Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = sts},\n222: \t\t\t\t},\n223: \t\t\t}\n224: \t\t\tfitErr.Diagnosis.AddPluginStatus(sts)\n225: \t\t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, plugins.\n231: \trunPermitStatus := fwk.RunPermitPlugins(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n232: \tif !runPermitStatus.IsWait() && !runPermitStatus.IsSuccess() {\n233: \t\t// trigger un-reserve to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n234: \t\tfwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n235: \t\tif forgetErr := sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\n236: \t\t\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \"Scheduler cache ForgetPod failed\")\n237: \t\t}\n238: \n239: \t\tif runPermitStatus.IsRejected() {\n240: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n241: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n242: \t\t\t\tPod:         pod,\n243: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n244: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap: framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: runPermitStatus},\n245: \t\t\t\t},\n246: \t\t\t}\n247: \t\t\tfitErr.Diagnosis.AddPluginStatus(runPermitStatus)\n248: \t\t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, framework.NewStatus(runPermitStatus.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\n249: \t\t}\n250: \n251: \t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, runPermitStatus\n252: \t}\n253: \n254: \t// At the end of a successful scheduling cycle, pop and move up Pods if needed.\n255: \tif len(podsToActivate.Map) != 0 {\n256: \t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Activate(logger, podsToActivate.Map)\n257: \t\t// Clear the entries after activation.\n258: \t\tpodsToActivate.Map = make(map[string]*v1.Pod)\n259: \t}\n260: \n261: \treturn scheduleResult, assumedPodInfo, nil\n262: }\n263: \n264: // bindingCycle tries to bind an assumed Pod.\n265: func (sched *Scheduler) bindingCycle(\n266: \tctx context.Context,\n267: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n268: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n269: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n270: \tassumedPodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n271: \tstart time.Time,\n272: \tpodsToActivate *framework.PodsToActivate) *framework.Status {\n273: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n274: \n275: \tassumedPod := assumedPodInfo.Pod\n276: \n277: \t// Run \"permit\" plugins.\n278: \tif status := fwk.WaitOnPermit(ctx, assumedPod); !status.IsSuccess() {\n279: \t\tif status.IsRejected() {\n280: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n281: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n282: \t\t\t\tPod:         assumedPodInfo.Pod,\n283: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n284: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap:      framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: status},\n285: \t\t\t\t\tUnschedulablePlugins: sets.New(status.Plugin()),\n286: \t\t\t\t},\n287: \t\t\t}\n288: \t\t\treturn framework.NewStatus(status.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\n289: \t\t}\n290: \t\treturn \t}\n302: \n303: \t// Calculating nodeResourceString can be heavy. Avoid it if klog verbosity is below 2.\n304: \tlogger.V(2).Info(\"Successfully bound pod to node\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(assumedPod), \"node\", scheduleResult.SuggestedHost, \"evaluatedNodes\", scheduleResult.EvaluatedNodes, \"feasibleNodes\", scheduleResult.FeasibleNodes)\n305: \tmetrics.PodScheduled(fwk.ProfileName(), metrics.SinceInSeconds(start))\n306: \tmetrics.PodSchedulingAttempts.Observe(float64(assumedPodInfo.Attempts))\n307: \tif assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp != nil {\n308: \t\tmetrics.PodSchedulingDuration.WithLabelValues(getAttemptsLabel(assumedPodInfo)).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(*assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp))\n309: \t\tmetrics.PodSchedulingSLIDuration.WithLabelValues(getAttemptsLabel(assumedPodInfo)).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(*assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp))\n310: \t}\n311: \t// Run \"postbind\" plugins.\n312: \tfwk.RunPostBindPlugins(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n313: \n314: \t// At the end of a successful binding cycle, move up Pods if needed.\n315: \tif len(podsToActivate.Map) != 0 {\n316: \t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Activate(logger, podsToActivate.Map)\n317: \t\t// Unlike the logic in schedulingCycle(), we don't bother deleting the entries\n318: \t\t// as `podsToActivate.Map` is no longer consumed.\n319: \t}\n320: \n321: \treturn nil\n322: }\n323: \n324: func (sched *Scheduler) handleBindingCycleError(\n325: \tctx context.Context,\n326: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n327: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n328: \tpodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n329: \tstart time.Time,\n330: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n331: \tstatus *framework.Status) {\n332: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n333: \n334: \tassumedPod := podInfo.Pod\n335: \t// trigger un-reserve plugins to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n336: \tfwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n337: \tif forgetErr := sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\n338: \t\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \"scheduler cache ForgetPod failed\")\n339: \t} else {\n340: \t\t// \"Forget\"ing an assumed Pod in binding cycle should be treated as a PodDelete event,\n341: \t\t// as the assumed Pod had occupied a certain amount of resources in scheduler cache.\n342: \t\t//\n343: \t\t// Avoid moving the assumed Pod itself as it's always Unschedulable.\n344: \t\t// It's intentional to \"defer\" this operation; otherwise MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue() would\n345: \t\t// add this event to in-flight events and thus move the assumed pod to backoffQ anyways if the plugins don't have appropriate QueueingHint.\n346: \t\tif status.IsRejected() {\n347: \t\t\tdefer sched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, func(pod *v1.Pod) bool {\n348: \t\t\t\treturn assumedPod.UID != pod.UID\n349: \t\t\t})\n350: \t\t} else {\n351: \t\t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, nil)\n352: \t\t}\n353: \t}\n354: \n355: \tsched.FailureHandler(ctx, fwk, podInfo, status, clearNominatedNode, start)\n356: }\n357: \n358: func (sched *Scheduler) frameworkForPod(pod *v1.Pod) (framework.Framework, error) {\n359: \tfwk, ok := sched.Profiles[pod.Spec.SchedulerName]\n360: \tif !ok {\n361: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"profile not found for scheduler name %q\", pod.Spec.SchedulerName)\n362: \t}\n363: \treturn fwk, nil\n364: }\n365: \n366: // skipPodSchedule returns true if we could skip scheduling the pod for specified cases.\n367: func (sched *Scheduler) skipPodSchedule(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, pod *v1.Pod) bool {\n368: \t// Case 1: pod is being deleted.\n369: \tif pod.DeletionTimestamp != nil {\n370: \t\tfwk.EventRecorder().Eventf(pod, nil, v1.EventTypeWarning, \"FailedScheduling\", \"Scheduling\", \"skip schedule deleting pod: %v/%v\", pod.Namespace, pod.Name)\n371: node list.\n388: // If it succeeds, it will return the name of the node.\n389: // If it fails, it will return a FitError with reasons.\n390: func (sched *Scheduler) schedulePod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (result ScheduleResult, err error) {\n391: \ttrace := utiltrace.New(\"Scheduling\", utiltrace.Field{Key: \"namespace\", Value: pod.Namespace}, utiltrace.Field{Key: \"name\", Value: pod.Name})\n392: \tdefer trace.LogIfLong(100 * time.Millisecond)\n393: \tif err := sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot(klog.FromContext(ctx), sched.nodeInfoSnapshot); err != nil {\n394: \t\treturn result, err\n395: \t}\n396: \ttrace.Step(\"Snapshotting scheduler cache and node infos done\")\n397: \n398: \tif sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NumNodes() == 0 {\n399: \t\treturn result, ErrNoNodesAvailable\n400: \t}\n401: \n402: \tfeasibleNodes, diagnosis, err := sched.findNodesThatFitPod(ctx, fwk, state, pod)\n403: \tif err != nil {\n404: \t\treturn result, err\n405: \t}\n406: \ttrace.Step(\"Computing predicates done\")\n407: \n408: \tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n409: \t\treturn result, &framework.FitError{\n410: \t\t\tPod:         pod,\n411: \t\t\tNumAllNodes: sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NumNodes(),\n412: \t\t\tDiagnosis:   diagnosis,\n413: \t\t}\n414: \t}\n415: \n416: \t// When only one \ttrace.Step(\"Prioritizing done\")\n432: \n433: \treturn ScheduleResult{\n434: \t\tSuggestedHost:  host,\n435: \t\tEvaluatedNodes: len(feasibleNodes) + len(diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap),\n436: \t\tFeasibleNodes:  len(feasibleNodes),\n437: \t}, err\n438: }\n439: \n440: // Filters the nodes to find the ones that fit the pod based on the framework\n441: // filter plugins and filter extenders.\n442: func (sched *Scheduler) findNodesThatFitPod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, framework.Diagnosis, error) {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NodeInfos().List()\n449: \tif err != nil {\n450: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n451: \t}\n452: \t// Run \"prefilter\" plugins.\n453: \tpreRes, s := fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins(ctx, state, pod)\n454: \tif !s.IsSuccess() {\n455: \t\tif !s.IsRejected() {\n456: \t\t\treturn nil, diagnosis, s.AsError()\n457: \t\t}\n458: \t\t// All nodes in NodeToStatusMap will have the same status so that they can be handled in the preemption.\n459: \t\t// Some non trivial refactoring is needed to avoid this copy.\n460: \t\tfor _, n := range allNodes {\n461: \t\t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[n.Node().Name] = s\n462: \t\t}\n463: \n464: \t\t// Record the messages from PreFilter in Diagnosis.PreFilterMsg.\n465: \t\tmsg := s.Message()\n466: \t\tdiagnosis.PreFilterMsg = msg\n467: \t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Status after running PreFilter plugins for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"status\", msg)\n468: \t\tdiagnosis.AddPluginStatus(s)\n469: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, nil\n470: \t}\n471: \n472: \t// \"NominatedNodeName\" can potentially be set in a previous scheduling cycle as a result of preemption.\n473: \t// This node is likely the only candidate that will fit the pod, and hence we try it first before iterating over all nodes.\n474: \tif len(pod.Status.NominatedNodeName) > 0 {\n475: \t\tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.evaluateNominatedNode(ctx, pod, fwk, state, diagnosis)\n476: \t\tif err != nil {\n477: \t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Evaluation failed on nominated node\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"node\", pod.Status.NominatedNodeName)\n478: \t\t}\n479: \t\t// Nominated node passes all the filters, scheduler is good to assign this node to the pod.\n480: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) != 0 {\n481: \t\t\treturn feasibleNodes, diagnosis, nil\n482: \t\t}\n483: \t}\n484: \n485: \tnodes := allNodes\n486: \tif !preRes.AllNodes() {\n487: \t\tnodes = make([]*framework.NodeInfo, 0, len(preRes.NodeNames))\n488: \t\tfor _, n := range allNodes {\n489: \t\t\tif !preRes.NodeNames.Has(n.Node().Name) {\n490: \t\t\t\t// We consider Nodes that are filtered out by PreFilterResult as rejected via UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n491: \t\t\t\t// We have to record them in NodeToStatusMap so that they won't be considered as candidates in the preemption.\n492: \t\t\t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[n.Node().Name] = framework.NewStatus(framework.UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, \"node is filtered out by the prefilter result\")\n493: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n494: \t\t\t}\n495: \t\t\tnodes = append(nodes, n)\n496: \t\t}\n497: \t}\n498: \tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.findNodesThatPassFilters(ctx, fwk, state, pod, &diagnosis, nodes)\n499: \t// always try to update the sched.nextStartNodeIndex regardless of whether an error has occurred\n500: \t// this is helpful to make sure that all the nodes have a chance to be searched\n501: \tprocessedNodes := len(feasibleNodes) + len(diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n502: \tsched.nextStartNodeIndex = (sched.nextStartNodeIndex + processedNodes) % len(nodes)\n503: \tif err != nil {\n504: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n505: \t}\n506: \n507: \tfeasibleNodesAfterExtender, err := findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx, sched.Extenders, pod, feasibleNodes, diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n508: \tif err != nil {\n509: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n510: \t}\n511: \tif len(feasibleNodesAfterExtender) != len(feasibleNodes) {\n512: \t\t// Extenders filtered out some nodes.\n513: \t\t//\n514: \t\t// Extender doesn't support any kind of requeueing feature like EnqueueExtensions in the scheduling framework.\n515: \t\t// When Extenders reject some Nodes and the pod ends up being unschedulable,\n516: \t\t// we put framework.ExtenderName to pInfo.UnschedulablePlugins.\n517: \t\t// This Pod will be requeued from unschedulable pod pool to activeQ/backoffQ\n518: \t\t// by any kind of cluster events.\n519: \t\t// https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/122019\n520: \t\tif diagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins == nil {\n521: \t\t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins = sets.New[string]()\n522: \t\t}\n523: \t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins.Insert(framework.ExtenderName)\n524: \t}\n525: \n526: \treturn feasibleNodesAfterExtender, diagnosis, nil\n527: }\n528: \n529: func (sched *Scheduler) evaluateNominatedNode(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, diagnosis framework.Diagnosis) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n530: \tnnn := nil\n547: }\n548: \n549: // hasScoring checks if scoring nodes is configured.\n550: func (sched *Scheduler) hasScoring(fwk framework.Framework) bool {\n551: \tif fwk.HasScorePlugins() {\n552: \n562: // hasExtenderFilters checks if any extenders filter nodes.\n563: func (sched *Scheduler) hasExtenderFilters() bool {\n564: \tfor _, extender := range sched.Extenders {\n565: \t\tif *Scheduler) findNodesThatPassFilters(\n574: \tctx context.Context,\n575: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n576: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n577: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n578: \tdiagnosis *framework.Diagnosis,\n579: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n580: \tnumAllNodes := len(nodes)\n581: \tnumNodesToFind := sched.numFeasibleNodesToFind(fwk.PercentageOfNodesToScore(), int32(numAllNodes))\n582: \tif !sched.hasExtenderFilters() && !sched.hasScoring(fwk) {\n583: \t\tnumNodesToFind = 1\n584: \t}\n585: \n586: \t// Create feasible list with enough space to avoid growing it\n587: \t// and allow assigning.\n588: \tfeasibleNodes := make([]*framework.NodeInfo, numNodesToFind)\n589: \n590: \tif \t}\n596: \n597: \terrCh := parallelize.NewErrorChannel()\n598: \tvar feasibleNodesLen int32\n599: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n600: \tdefer cancel()\n601: \n602: \ttype nodeStatus struct {\n603: \t\tnode   string\n604: \t\tstatus *framework.Status\n605: \t}\n606: \tresult := make([]*nodeStatus, numAllNodes)\n607: \tcheckNode := func(i int) {\n608: \t\t// We check the nodes starting from where we left off in the previous scheduling cycle,\n609: \t\t// this is to make sure all nodes have the same chance of being examined across pods.\n610: \t\tnodeInfo := nodes[(sched.nextStartNodeIndex+i)%numAllNodes]\n611: \t\tstatus := fwk.RunFilterPluginsWithNominatedPods(ctx, state, pod, nodeInfo)\n612: \t\tif status.Code() == framework.Error {\n613: \t\t\terrCh.SendErrorWithCancel(status.AsError(), cancel)\n614: \t\t\treturn\n615: \t\t}\n616: \t\tif status.IsSuccess() {\n617: \t\t\tlength := atomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, 1)\n618: \t\t\tif length > numNodesToFind {\n619: \t\t\t\tcancel()\n620: \t\t\t\tatomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, -1)\n621: \t\t\t} else {\n622: \t\t\t\tfeasibleNodes[length-1] = nodeInfo\n623: \t\t\t}\n624: \t\t} else {\n625: \t\t\tresult[i] = &nodeStatus{node: nodeInfo.Node().Name, status: status}\n626: \t\t}\n627: \t}\n628: \n629: \tbeginCheckNode := time.Now()\n630: \tstatusCode := framework.Success\n631: \tdefer func() {\n632: \t\t// We record Filter extension point latency here instead of in framework.go because framework.RunFilterPlugins\n633: \t\t// function is called for each node, whereas we want to have an overall latency for all nodes per scheduling cycle.\n634: \t\t// Note that this latency also includes latency for `addNominatedPods`, which calls framework.RunPreFilterAddPod.\n635: \t\tmetrics.FrameworkExtensionPointDuration.WithLabelValues(metrics.Filter, statusCode.String(), fwk.ProfileName()).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(beginCheckNode))\n636: \t}()\n637: \n638: \t// Stops searching for more nodes once the configured number of feasible nodes\n639: \t// are found.\n640: \tfwk.Parallelizer().Until(ctx, numAllNodes, checkNode, metrics.Filter)\n641: \tfeasibleNodes = feasibleNodes[:feasibleNodesLen]\n642: \tfor _, item := range result {\n643: \t\tif item == nil {\n644: \t\t\tcontinue\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[item.node] = item.status\n647: \t\tdiagnosis.AddPluginStatus(item.status)\n648: \t}\n649: \tif err := errCh.ReceiveError(); err != nil {\n650: \t\tstatusCode = framework.Error\n651: \t\treturn feasibleNodes, err\n652: \t}\n653: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n654: }\n655: \n656: // numFeasibleNodesToFind returns the number of feasible nodes that once found, the scheduler stops\n657: // its search for more feasible nodes.\n658: func (sched *Scheduler) numFeasibleNodesToFind(percentageOfNodesToScore *int32, numAllNodes int32) (numNodes int32) {\n659: \tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n660: \t\treturn numAllNodes\n661: \t}\n662: \n663: \t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. Otherwise, use global percentageOfNodesToScore.\n664: \tvar percentage int32\n665: \tif percentageOfNodesToScore != nil {\n666: \t\tpercentage = *percentageOfNodesToScore\n667: \t} else {\n668: \t\tpercentage = sched.percentageOfNodesToScore\n669: \t}\n670: \n671: \tif percentage == 0 {\n672: \t\tpercentage = int32(50) - numAllNodes/125\n673: \t\tif percentage < minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind {\n674: \t\t\tpercentage = minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind\n675: \t\t}\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tnumNodes = numAllNodes * percentage / 100\n679: \tif numNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n680: \t\treturn minFeasibleNodesToFind\n681: \t}\n682: \n683: \treturn numNodes\n684: }\n685: \n686: func findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx context.Context, extenders []framework.Extender, pod *v1.Pod, feasibleNodes []*framework.NodeInfo, statuses framework.NodeToStatusMap) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n687: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n688: \t// Extenders are called sequentially.\n689: \t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\n690: \t// extender in a decreasing manner.\n691: \tfor _, extender := range extenders {\n692: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n693: \t\t\tbreak\n694: \t\t}\n695: \t\tif !extender.IsInterested(pod) {\n696: \t\t\tcontinue\n697: \t\t}\n698: \n699: \t\t// Status of failed nodes in failedAndUnresolvableMap will be added or overwritten in <statuses>,\n700: \t\t// so that the scheduler framework can respect the UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status for\n701: \t\t// particular nodes, and this may eventually improve preemption efficiency.\n702: \t\t// Note: users are recommended to configure the extenders that may return UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n703: \t\t// status ahead of others.\n704: \t\tfeasibleList, failedMap, failedAndUnresolvableMap, err := extender.Filter(pod, feasibleNodes)\n705: \t\tif err != nil \\n118: // QueueingHintFn returns a hint that signals whether the event can make a Pod,\\n119: // which was rejected by this plugin in the past scheduling cycle, schedulable or not.\\n120: // It's int64\\n42: \\n43: // ActionType is an integer to represent one type of resource change.\\n44: // Different ActionTypes can be bit-wised to compose new semantics.\\n45: type ActionType int64\\n46: \\n47: // Constants for ActionTypes.\\n48: const (\\n49: \\tAdd    ActionType = 1 << iota // 1\\n50: \\tDelete                        // 10\\n51: \\t// UpdateNodeXYZ is only applicable for Node events.\\n52: \\tUpdateNodeAllocatable // 100\\n53: \\tUpdateNodeLabel       // 1000\\n54: \\tUpdateNodeTaint       // 10000\\n55: \\tUpdateNodeCondition   // 100000\\n56: \\tUpdateNodeAnnotation  // 1000000\\n57: \\n58: \\tAll ActionType = 1<<iota - 1 // 1111111\\n59: \\n60: \\t// Use the general Update type if you don't either know or care the specific sub-Update type to use.\\n61: \\tUpdate = UpdateNodeAllocatable | UpdateNodeLabel | UpdateNodeTaint | UpdateNodeCondition | UpdateNodeAnnotation\\n62: )\\n63: \\n64: // GVK is short for group/version/kind, which can uniquely represent a particular API resource.\\n65: type GVK string\\n66: \\n67: // Constants for GVKs.\\n68: const (\\n69: \\t// There are a couple of notes about how the scheduler notifies the events of Pods:\\n70: \\t// - Add: add events could be triggered by either a newly created Pod or an existing Pod that is scheduled to a Node.\\n71: \\t// - Delete: delete events could be triggered by:\\n72: \\t//           - a Pod that is deleted\\n73: \\t//           - a Pod that was assumed, but gets un-assumed due to some errors in the binding cycle.\\n74: \\t//           - an existing Pod that was unscheduled but gets scheduled to a Node.\\n75: \\tPod GVK = \\\"Pod\\\"\\n76: \\t// A note about NodeAdd event and UpdateNodeTaint event:\\n77: \\t// NodeAdd QueueingHint isn't always called because of the internal feature called preCheck.\\n78: \\t// It's definitely not something expected for plugin developers,\\n79: \\t// and registering UpdateNodeTaint event is the only mitigation for now.\\n80: \\t// So, kube-scheduler registers UpdateNodeTaint event for plugins that has NodeAdded event, but don't have UpdateNodeTaint event.\\n81: \\t// It has a bad impact for the requeuing efficiency though, a lot better than some Pods being stuck in the\\n82: \\t// unschedulable pod pool.\\n83: \\t// This behavior will be removed when we remove the preCheck feature.\\n84: \\t// See: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\\n85: \\tNode                    GVK = \\\"Node\\\"\\n86: \\tPersistentVolume        GVK = \\\"PersistentVolume\\\"\\n87: \\tPersistentVolumeClaim   GVK = \\\"PersistentVolumeClaim\\\"\\n88: \\tCSINode                 GVK = \\\"storage.k8s.io/CSINode\\\"\\n89: \\tCSIDriver               GVK = \\\"storage.k8s.io/CSIDriver\\\"\\n90: \\tCSIStorageCapacity      GVK = \\\"storage.k8s.io/CSIStorageCapacity\\\"\\n91: \\tStorageClass            GVK = \\\"storage.k8s.io/StorageClass\\\"\\n92: \\tPodSchedulingContext    GVK = \\\"PodSchedulingContext\\\"\\n93: \\tResourceClaim           GVK = \\\"ResourceClaim\\\"\\n94: \\tResourceClass           GVK = \\\"ResourceClass\\\"\\n95: \\tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \\\"ResourceClaimParameters\\\"\\n96: \\tResourceClassParameters GVK = \\\"ResourceClassParameters\\\"\\n97: \\n98: \\t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\\n99: \\t// e.g., If you register `{Resource: \\\"*\\\", ActionType: All}` in EventsToRegister,\\n100: \\t// all coming clusterEvents will be admitted. Be careful to register it, it will\\n101: \\t// increase the computing pressure in requeueing unless you really need it.\\n102: \\t//\\n103: \\t// Meanwhile, if the coming clusterEvent is a wildcard one, all pods\\n104: \\t// will be moved from unschedulablePod pool to activeQ/backoffQ forcibly.\\n105: \\tWildCard GVK = \\\"*\\\"\\n106: )\\n107: \\n108: type ClusterEventWithHint struct {\\n109: \\tEvent ClusterEvent\\n110: \\t// QueueingHintFn is executed for the plugin rejected by this plugin when the above Event happens,\\n111: \\t// and filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\\n112: \\t// It's an optional field. If not set,\\n113: \\t// the scheduling of Pods will be always retried with backoff when this Event happens.\\n114: \\t// (the same as Queue)\\n115: \\tQueueingHintFn QueueingHintFn\\n116: }\\n117: \\n118: // QueueingHintFn returns a hint that signals whether the event can make a Pod,\\n119: // which was rejected by this plugin in the past scheduling cycle, schedulable or not.\\n120: // It's called before a Pod gets moved from unschedulableQ to backoffQ or activeQ.\\n121: // If it returns an error, we'll take the returned QueueingHint as `Queue` at the caller whatever we returned here so that\\n122: // we can prevent the Pod from being stuck in the unschedulable pod pool.\\n123: //\\n124: // - `pod`: the Pod to be enqueued, which is rejected by this plugin in the past.\\n125: // - `oldObj` `newObj`: the object involved in that event.\\n126: //   - For example, the given event is \\\"Node deleted\\\", the `oldObj` will be that deleted Node.\\n127: //   - `oldObj` is nil if the event is add event.\\n128: //   - `newObj` is nil if the event is delete event.\\n129: type QueueingHintFn func(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (QueueingHint, error)\\n130: \\n131: type QueueingHint int\\n132: \\n133: const (\\n134: \\t// QueueSkip implies that the cluster event has no impact on\\n135: \\t// scheduling of the pod.\\n136: \\tQueueSkip QueueingHint = iota\\n137: \\n138: \\t// Queue implies that the Pod may be schedulable by the event.\\n139: \\tQueue\\n140: )\\n141: \\n142: func (s QueueingHint) String() string {\\n143: \\tswitch s {\\n144: \\tcase QueueSkip:\\n145: \\t\\treturn \\\"QueueSkip\\\"\\n146: \\tcase Queue:\\n147: \\t\\treturn \\\"Queue\\\"\\n148: \\t}\\n149: \\treturn \\\"\\\"\\n150: }\\n151: \\n152: // ClusterEvent abstracts how a system resource's state gets changed.\\n153: // Resource represents the standard API resources such as Pod, Node, etc.\\n154: // ActionType denotes the specific change such as Add, Update or Delete.\\n155: type ClusterEvent struct {\\n156: \\tResource   GVK\\n157: \\tActionType ActionType\\n158: \\tLabel      string\\n159: }\\n160: \\n161: // IsWildCard returns true if ClusterEvent follows WildCard semantics\\n162: func (ce ClusterEvent) IsWildCard() bool {\\n163: \\treturn ce.Resource == WildCard && ce.ActionType == All\\n164: }\\n165: \\n166: // Match returns true if ClusterEvent is matched with the coming event.\\n167: // If the ce.Resource is \\\"*\\\", there's no requirement for the coming event' Resource.\\n168: // Contrarily, if the coming event's Resource is \\\"*\\\", the ce.Resource should only be \\\"*\\\".\\n169: //\\n170: // Note: we have a special case here when the coming event is a wildcard event,\\n171: // it will force all Pods to move to bit-wised to compose new semantics.\n45: type ActionType int64\n46: \n47: // Constants for ActionTypes.\n48: const (\n49: \tAdd    ActionType = 1 << iota // 1\n50: \tDelete                        // 10\n51: \t// UpdateNodeXYZ is only applicable for Node events.\n52: \tUpdateNodeAllocatable // 100\n53: \tUpdateNodeLabel       // 1000\n54: \tUpdateNodeTaint       // 10000\n55: \tUpdateNodeCondition   // 100000\n56: \tUpdateNodeAnnotation  // 1000000\n57: \n58: \tAll ActionType = 1<<iota - 1 // 1111111\n59: \n60: \t// Use the general Update type if you don't either know or care the specific sub-Update type to use.\n61: \tUpdate = UpdateNodeAllocatable | UpdateNodeLabel | UpdateNodeTaint | UpdateNodeCondition | UpdateNodeAnnotation\n62: )\n63: \n64: // GVK is short for group/version/kind, which can uniquely represent a particular API resource.\n65: type GVK string\n66: \n67: // Constants for GVKs.\n68: const (\n69: \t// There are a couple of notes about how the scheduler notifies the events of Pods:\n70: \t// - Add: add events could be triggered by either a newly created Pod or an existing Pod that is scheduled to a Node.\n71: \t// - Delete: delete events could be triggered by:\n72: \t//           - a Pod that is deleted\n73: \t//           - a Pod that was assumed, but gets un-assumed due to some errors in the binding cycle.\n74: \t//           - an existing Pod that was unscheduled but gets scheduled to a Node.\n75: \tPod GVK = \"Pod\"\n76: \t// A note about NodeAdd event and UpdateNodeTaint event:\n77: \t// NodeAdd QueueingHint isn't always called because of the internal feature called preCheck.\n78: \t// It's definitely not something expected for plugin developers,\n79: \t// and registering UpdateNodeTaint event is the only mitigation for now.\n80: \t// So, kube-scheduler registers UpdateNodeTaint event for plugins that has NodeAdded event, but don't have UpdateNodeTaint event.\n81: \t// It has a bad impact for the requeuing efficiency though, a lot better than some Pods being stuck in the\n82: \t// unschedulable pod pool.\n83: \t// This behavior will be removed when we remove the preCheck feature.\n84: \t// See: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\n85: \tNode                    GVK = \"Node\"\n86: \tPersistentVolume        GVK = \"PersistentVolume\"\n87: \tPersistentVolumeClaim   GVK = \"PersistentVolumeClaim\"\n88: \tCSINode                 GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/CSINode\"\n89: \tCSIDriver               GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/CSIDriver\"\n90: \tCSIStorageCapacity      GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/CSIStorageCapacity\"\n91: \tStorageClass            GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/StorageClass\"\n92: \tPodSchedulingContext    GVK = \"PodSchedulingContext\"\n93: \tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n94: \tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n95: \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n96: \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n97: \n98: \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n99: \t// e.g., If you register `{Resource: \"*\", ActionType: All}` in EventsToRegister,\n100: \t// all coming clusterEvents will be admitted. Be careful to register it, it will\n101: \t// increase the computing pressure in requeueing unless you really need it.\n102: \t//\n103: \t// Meanwhile, if the coming clusterEvent is a wildcard one, all pods\n104: \t// will be moved from unschedulablePod pool to activeQ/backoffQ forcibly.\n105: \tWildCard GVK = \"*\"\n106: )\n107: \n108: type ClusterEventWithHint struct {\n109: \tEvent ClusterEvent\n110: \t// QueueingHintFn is executed for the plugin rejected by this plugin when the above Event happens,\n111: \t// and filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\n112: \t// It's an optional field. If not set,\n113: \t// the scheduling of Pods will be always retried with backoff when this Event happens.\n114: \t// (the same as Queue)\n115: \tQueueingHintFn QueueingHintFn\n116: }\n117: \n118: // QueueingHintFn returns a hint that signals whether the event can make a Pod,\n119: // which was rejected by this plugin in the past scheduling cycle, schedulable or not.\n120: // It's called before a Pod gets moved from unschedulableQ to backoffQ or activeQ.\n121: // If it returns an error, we'll take the returned QueueingHint as `Queue` at the caller whatever we returned here so that\n122: // we can prevent the Pod from being stuck in the unschedulable pod pool.\n123: //\n124: // - `pod`: the Pod to be enqueued, which is rejected by this plugin in the past.\n125: // - `oldObj` `newObj`: the object involved in that event.\n126: //   - For example, the given event is \"Node deleted\", the `oldObj` will be that deleted Node.\n127: //   - `oldObj` is nil if the event is add event.\n128: //   - `newObj` is nil if the event is delete event.\n129: type QueueingHintFn func(logger klog.Logger, pod *v1.Pod, oldObj, newObj interface{}) (QueueingHint, error)\n130: \n131: type QueueingHint \t\t// Add the messages from PreFilter plugins to reasonMsg.\n380: \t\treasonMsg += fmt.Sprintf(\" %v.\", preFilterMsg)\n381: \t}\n382: \n383: \tif preFilterMsg == \"\" {\n384: \t\t// the scheduling cycle went through PreFilter extension point successfully.\n385: \t\t//\n386: \t\t// When the prefilter plugin returns unschedulable,\n387: \t\t// the scheduling framework inserts the same I now have a comprehensive understanding of the bug. Let me create a summary document:\n\n**Root Cause:**\nThe bug is that ResourceSlice events are not registered for the scheduling queue's re-evaluation mechanism. When a ResourceSlice is created or updated (which happens when a DRA driver starts and publishes resource availability), the scheduler doesn't know to re-evaluate pods that previously failed due to missing ResourceSlices.\n\n**Where the bug occurs:**\n\n1. **Missing GVK constant in `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`** - ResourceSlice is not defined as a GVK constant and not included in `UnrollWildCardResource()`\n\n2. **Missing event handler registration in `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`** - In the `addAllEventHandlers()` function, there's no case for framework.ResourceSlice\n\n3. **Missing event registration in `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`** - The `EventsToRegister()` function doesn't include ResourceSlice events\n\n**The fix:**\n1. calls `ScheduleOne()` which invokes `schedulingCycle()` that calls `SchedulePod()`, which eventually checks resource allocation status\n- `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` — Registers event handlers for cluster resources; examined the `addAllEventHandlers()` function that sets up handlers for various resource types including Dynamic Resource Allocation resources\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` — Defines GVK (Group/Version/Kind) constants for all supported resource types and the `UnrollWildCardResource()` function\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` — DRA plugin that checks resource availability; examined the `EventsToRegister()` method that returns events that should trigger pod rescheduling\n- `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` — Scheduler initialization (referenced for context)\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/api/resource/v1alpha2/types.go` — ResourceSlice API type definition (confirmed it exists)\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:111` — `schedulingCycle()` calls `SchedulePod()` which executes the plugin chain\n2. **Plugin evaluation**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go:418-423` — `PreEnqueue()` checks if all resource claims can be allocated\n3. **Filter execution**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` — Filter phase checks if resources are available on nodes\n4. **Event registration**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go:381-413` — `EventsToRegister()` specifies which cluster events should trigger pod rescheduling\n5. **Event handler setup**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go:287-546` — `addAllEventHandlers()` registers informer handlers for cluster resource events\n6. **GVK definition missing**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go:64-106` — ResourceSlice is not defined as a framework GVK\n7. **Bug triggered**: When a ResourceSlice is created/updated after a pod fails scheduling, **no event handler exists to notify the scheduler queue**\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n**Function**: GVK constant definitions and `UnrollWildCardResource()`\n**Line**: ~92-106 and ~177-193\n**Explanation**:\n\nThe framework is missing a GVK constant for ResourceSlice. Although ResourceSlice objects exist in the Kubernetes API and are used by the DRA plugin to track available resources, they are not registered as a recognized cluster event type. This causes two downstream problems:\n\n1. **Missing GVK constant** (line 92-96): The following GVK constants are defined for DRA:\n   - `PodSchedulingContext`\n   - `ResourceClaim`\n   - `ResourceClass`\n   - `ResourceClaimParameters`\n   - `ResourceClassParameters`\n   - **But NOT `ResourceSlice`**\n\n2. **Missing in UnrollWildCardResource()** (line 187-191): The function that expands wildcard events includes ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, etc., but **NOT ResourceSlice**.\n\nThis cascades into two additional files where ResourceSlice events cannot be properly handled:\n\n**Secondary Issue**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go:395-543`\n- The `addAllEventHandlers()` function has a switch statement that handles GVK types\n- It has cases for ResourceClass, ResourceClaimParameters, ResourceClassParameters, etc.\n- **But no case for ResourceSlice** — so even if ResourceSlice was a valid GVK, no informer handler would be registered\n\n**Tertiary Issue**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go:381-413`\n- The `EventsToRegister()` method returns events that should trigger pod rescheduling\n- It includes: ResourceClaimParameters, ResourceClassParameters, ResourceClaim, PodSchedulingContext, Node, ResourceClass\n- **But NOT ResourceSlice** — so the plugin never signals the scheduler queue to retry pods when ResourceSlices are created/updated\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n\n```diff\nconst (\n\tPod GVK = \"Pod\"\n\tNode                    GVK = \"Node\"\n\tPersistentVolume        GVK = \"PersistentVolume\"\n\tPersistentVolumeClaim   GVK = \"PersistentVolumeClaim\"\n\tCSINode                 GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/CSINode\"\n\tCSIDriver               GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/CSIDriver\"\n\tCSIStorageCapacity      GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/CSIStorageCapacity\"\n\tStorageClass            GVK = \"storage.k8s.io/StorageClass\"\n\tPodSchedulingContext    GVK = \"PodSchedulingContext\"\n\tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n\tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n\tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n\tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n\tWildCard GVK = \"*\"\n)\n```\n\n### Fix 2: Add ResourceSlice to UnrollWildCardResource()\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n\n```diff\nfunc UnrollWildCardResource() []ClusterEventWithHint {\n\treturn []ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Pod, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: Node, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolume, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PersistentVolumeClaim, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSINode, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIDriver, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: CSIStorageCapacity, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: StorageClass, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaim, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClass, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: All}},\n\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: All}},\n+\t\t{Event: ClusterEvent{Resource: ResourceSlice, ActionType: All}},\n\t}\n}\n```\n\n### Fix 3: Add ResourceSlice event handler registration\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n\n```diff\n\tfor gvk, at := range gvkMap {\n\t\tswitch gvk {\n\t\tcase framework.Node, framework.Pod:\n\t\t\t// Do nothing.\n\t\tcase framework.CSINode:\n\t\t\t// ... handle CSINode ...\n\t\t// ... other cases ...\n\t\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n\t\t\t}\n+\t\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n\t\t\t// ... handle StorageClass ...\n```\n\n### Fix 4: Register ResourceSlice events in DRA plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n\n```diff\nfunc (pl *dynamicResources) EventsToRegister() []framework.ClusterEventWithHint {\n\tif !pl.enabled {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t// Changes for claim or class parameters creation may make pods\n\t\t// schedulable which depend on claims using those parameters.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimParametersChange},\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClassParametersChange},\n\n\t\t// Allocation is tracked in ResourceClaims, so any changes may make the pods schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaim, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimChange},\n\t\t// When a driver has provided additional information, a pod waiting for that information\n\t\t// may be schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange},\n\t\t// A resource might depend on node labels for topology filtering.\n\t\t// A new or updated node may make pods schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.UpdateNodeLabel | framework.UpdateNodeTaint}},\n\t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlices published by drivers contain available resources.\n+\t\t// A new or updated ResourceSlice may make pods schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n\t}\n\treturn events\n}\n```\n\n(Additionally, implement `pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange()` method with similar logic to other change detection methods.)\n\n## Analysis\n\n### The Bug's Lifecycle\n\n1. **Pod Creation**: A pod requesting DRA resources is created before the DRA driver starts\n2. **Initial Scheduling Attempt** (line ~111 in schedule_one.go):\n   - The scheduler calls `schedulingCycle()`\n   - The DRA plugin's PreEnqueue/Filter phases check for available ResourceSlices\n   - No ResourceSlices exist yet → pod marked as Unschedulable\n3. **Pod Queuing**: The pod is added to the unschedulable queue with the reason \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n4. **Driver Starts**: The DRA driver boots up and creates ResourceSlice objects to advertise available resources\n5. **ResourceSlice Events (BUG HERE)**:\n   - The ResourceSlice informer detects Add/Update events\n   - But there is **NO event handler registered** for ResourceSlice (missing from eventhandlers.go)\n   - Even if a handler existed, the **DRA plugin doesn't register for ResourceSlice events** (missing from EventsToRegister())\n6. **Pod Stuck**: The scheduler never re-evaluates the pod because no one told the scheduler queue that something relevant changed\n7. **Result**: Pod remains permanently in Unschedulable state despite resources now being available\n\n### Why This Happens\n\nThe scheduler uses an event-driven architecture where cluster resources can trigger re-evaluation of unschedulable pods. The mechanism works like this:\n\n1. When a pod fails scheduling, it's added to the `unschedulablePods` pool\n2. When relevant cluster events occur (e.g., Node resource changes), the scheduler queue is notified\n3. The queue calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to retry unschedulable pods\n4. For this to work, each plugin must register which events are relevant to it via `EventsToRegister()`\n5. The scheduler framework must have event handlers that listen to those events and signal the queue\n\nResourceSlice events are critical for DRA scheduling because:\n- ResourceSlices advertise node-local resources available to a driver\n- When a driver starts, it publishes ResourceSlices showing what resources it manages\n- Pods waiting for those resources need to be retried when the ResourceSlices appear\n- Without this wiring, pods become permanently stuck\n\nThe fix is to add ResourceSlice to all three layers of event handling in the scheduler.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":8,"cache_creation_input_tokens":11507,"cache_read_input_tokens":83227,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":11507},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"7c6c5bcd-2da2-4edd-bbf6-e1b1aa14b46e","uuid":"9568dda4-bfc1-45f3-9103-ea32d9e2d2f5"}

{\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n\t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n\t\t\t// ... handle StorageClass ...\n```\n\n### Fix 4: Register ResourceSlice events in DRA plugin\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n\n```diff\nfunc (pl *dynamicResources) EventsToRegister() []framework.ClusterEventWithHint {\n\tif !pl.enabled {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t// Changes for claim or class parameters creation may make pods\n\t\t// schedulable which depend on claims using those parameters.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimParametersChange},\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClassParametersChange},\n\n\t\t// Allocation is tracked in ResourceClaims, so any changes may make the pods schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaim, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimChange},\n\t\t// When a driver has provided additional information, a pod waiting for that information\n\t\t// may be schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange},\n\t\t// A resource might depend on node labels for topology filtering.\n\t\t// A new or updated node may make pods schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.UpdateNodeLabel | framework.UpdateNodeTaint}},\n\t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlices published by drivers contain available resources.\n+\t\t// A new or updated ResourceSlice may make pods schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n\t}\n\treturn events\n}\n```\n\n(Additionally, implement `pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange()` method with similar logic to other change detection methods.)\n\n## Analysis\n\n### The Bug's Lifecycle\n\n1. **Pod Creation**: A pod requesting DRA resources is created before the DRA driver starts\n2. **Initial Scheduling Attempt** (line ~111 in schedule_one.go):\n   - The scheduler calls `schedulingCycle()`\n   - The DRA plugin's PreEnqueue/Filter phases check for available ResourceSlices\n   - No ResourceSlices exist yet → pod marked as Unschedulable\n3. **Pod Queuing**: The pod is added to the unschedulable queue with the reason \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n4. **Driver Starts**: The DRA driver boots up and creates ResourceSlice objects to advertise available resources\n5. **ResourceSlice Events (BUG HERE)**:\n   - The ResourceSlice informer detects Add/Update events\n   - But there is **NO event handler registered** for ResourceSlice (missing from eventhandlers.go)\n   - Even if a handler existed, the **DRA plugin doesn't register for ResourceSlice events** (missing from EventsToRegister())\n6. **Pod Stuck**: The scheduler never re-evaluates the pod because no one told the scheduler queue that something relevant changed\n7. **Result**: Pod remains permanently in Unschedulable state despite resources now being available\n\n### Why This Happens\n\nThe scheduler uses an event-driven architecture where cluster resources can trigger re-evaluation of unschedulable pods. The mechanism works like this:\n\n1. When a pod fails scheduling, it's added to the `unschedulablePods` pool\n2. When relevant cluster events occur (e.g., Node resource changes), the scheduler queue is notified\n3. The queue calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` to retry unschedulable pods\n4. For this to work, each plugin must register which events are relevant to it via `EventsToRegister()`\n5. The scheduler framework must have event handlers that listen to those events and signal the queue\n\nResourceSlice events are critical for DRA scheduling because:\n- ResourceSlices advertise node-local resources available to a driver\n- When a driver starts, it publishes ResourceSlices showing what resources it manages\n- Pods waiting for those resources need to be retried when the ResourceSlices appear\n- Without this wiring, pods become permanently stuck\n\nThe fix is to add ResourceSlice to all three layers of event handling in the scheduler.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
